  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_49978889-9776-4ea6-8e10-5c59420d7799'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer16366353261983374300">For centuries, the people of Alera have relied on the power of the furies to protect them from outside invaders.   <span id="freeText16366353261983374300" style="display:none">For centuries, the people of Alera have relied on the power of the furies to protect them from outside invaders. But the gravest threat might be closer than they think.<br /><br />Tavi has escaped the Calderon Valley and the mysterious attack of the Marat on his homeland. But he is far from safe, as trying to keep up the illusion of being a student while secretly training as one of the First Lord's spies is a dangerous game. And he has not yet learned to use the furies, making him especially vulnerable.<br /><br />When the attack comes it's on two fronts. A sudden strike threatens the First Lord's life and threatens to plunge the land into civil war. While in the Calderon Valley, the threat faced from the Marat is dwarfed by an ancient menace. And Tavi must learn to harness the furies if he has any chance of fighting the greatest threat Alera has ever known . . .</span>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I think technically the taken were controlled by the little worm things (Takers) that crawl into their heads, the Queen in turn controlled the Takers.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I think technically the taken were controlled by the little worm things (Takers) that crawl into their heads, the Queen in turn controlled the Takers. <br /><br />With the Queen dead, the takers would still have control of the taken just without the unifying control of the Queen to command them, leaving them with little more than animalistic behaviour / continuing to follow the last given order.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>

<div id="review_2315378461" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2315378461" />
    <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus"><img alt="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588320656p2/78485297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2315378461?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus">Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus?shelf=butcher-jim">butcher-jim</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2315378461" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7598502448645836428">A good, old-fashioned fantasy series that doesn´t try to reinvent something, break with genre conventions, be progressive, but instead tells a great story, has a cool magic system, an interesting enemy and very good characterizations. <br/><br/>It has become a bit difficult for fantasy authors who don´t go the dark way and make everything grimmer and dirtier, but stay instead with a bit of the cheerful, Tolkien, happy go lucky style, reminiscing the good old days when bad was bad and good was good. <br/><br/>Some n</span>
  <span id="freeText7598502448645836428" style="display:none">A good, old-fashioned fantasy series that doesn´t try to reinvent something, break with genre conventions, be progressive, but instead tells a great story, has a cool magic system, an interesting enemy and very good characterizations. <br /><br />It has become a bit difficult for fantasy authors who don´t go the dark way and make everything grimmer and dirtier, but stay instead with a bit of the cheerful, Tolkien, happy go lucky style, reminiscing the good old days when bad was bad and good was good. <br /><br />Some not liking this series may be simply too strict with it, because not every novel can or want to be the next Rothfuss or Sanderson and I am sure that many are appreciating the conventional and entertaining way fantasy used to be told since just a few years ago. <br /><br />I like the mixture of ideas, the avatars, and elementary powers, the evil Vord that will become a cool, evil collective intelligence, something a bit closer to Sci-Fi than to Fantasy and a stylish, unusual enemy for the genre. <br /><br />Give the thing a chance, Butcher is a great storyteller and hey, one can never run out of fantasy series if there comes a time when nothing too seductive is waiting in the TBR. <br /><br />Tropes show how literature is conceptualized and created and which mixture of elements makes works and genres unique: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Creator/JimButcher">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Literature/CodexAlera">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7598502448645836428" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1792821256" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1792821256" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1792821256?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781841497457" href="/book/show/4961960-academ-s-fury">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1792821256" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8362972612575413786"><b>2.5/5 Stars<br/><br/>Another okay installment in the Codex Alera series, it’s time for me to part way with this series.</b><br/><br/>I’m going to keep this review short, I actually can copy my review for the first book here to explain why I won’t be continuing with this series. <br/><br/>Although my review is going to sound negative, let me state that this is not a bad series, but then again there’s nothing special about it and I don’t see any sign of improvement from the first book. It’s all once again, pretty basic and formula</span>
  <span id="freeText8362972612575413786" style="display:none"><b>2.5/5 Stars<br /><br />Another okay installment in the Codex Alera series, it’s time for me to part way with this series.</b><br /><br />I’m going to keep this review short, I actually can copy my review for the first book here to explain why I won’t be continuing with this series. <br /><br />Although my review is going to sound negative, let me state that this is not a bad series, but then again there’s nothing special about it and I don’t see any sign of improvement from the first book. It’s all once again, pretty basic and formulaic.<br /><br />I can already predict that the newly introduced villain in this book, the vord, will become the final boss of the series. Let me make a guess, the vord sounds like a virus so judging from that, there will be a Queen or King vord that became the final boss of the series. Then, judging from the tone of the series so far, even though there are war, politics and all that jazz, none of the main POV characters will die, maybe one at most. Feel free to correct me if I’m wrong.<br /><br />Academ’s Fury, the second book out of six in the Codex Alera series, began two years after the events of Furies of Calderon and the plot is still immensely predictable. A lot of scenes were still too long for the pacing’s own good and Butcher kept on repeating the things we already understood over and over again. For example, Amara couldn’t have a child. This situation is repeated for so many pages throughout the book. I don’t know why Butcher had the need to emphasize this point over and over again. I get it, she can’t have a child, saying it once or twice is enough. The worst part is, this is only one of many examples. Also, this series actually featured a lot of romance and I’m generally not a big fan of romance in my fantasy read.<br /><br />Characters are still very hard to care, I kept on wishing the entire plot to focus only on Tavi because his POV is the only one that I’m slightly invested in. The rest are just okay-ish to meh. Amara was probably the worst for me, I kept on wishing she would die already so I don’t have to read her POV anymore. Maybe when it comes down to it, I just couldn’t connect with Butcher’s prose. I feel like I should've cared more about some of the events that happened in the book but it just didn’t connect with me. I’ve read a few series that’s predictable but they still managed to intrigue and made me invested, but not Codex Alera.<br /><br />I’m usually a patient leader but still, there’s a limit to my patience. This is not a small series at all, six books long and each book are easily over 600 pages. I’ve read more or less 1300 pages so far and I’m only slightly invested in Tavi. That’s ONE character, only one over the course of 1300 pages and 400k+ words. If I’m not invested in the characters by this point, there’s just no way I can push myself to continue with the series. I tried so hard and got so farrrr, but in the enddd it doesn’t even matter. <br /><br />This is a beloved series among many, but when it doesn’t work, it just won’t work. I won’t be spending my time for another 3000 pages of an okay series, there are so many great books out there waiting for me. It's time for me to part ways with this series. Overall, this is a series that I would recommend only to anyone who’s new to adult fantasy.<br /><br /><i>You can find <b><a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/pat/913-academsfury" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a></b> and the rest of my Adult Epic/High Fantasy &amp; Sci-Fi reviews at <b><a href="http://booknest.eu/review/patrick" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNest</a></b></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="8362972612575413786" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2087561717" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">Pod People</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2087561717" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10325012280959640682">If you were on the fence about the first book (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1955069041' rel='nofollow noopener'>Furies of Calderon</a>) then go ahead and give this one a try. The pacing was faster, there are finally <i>some</i> explanations for the way the furies work, and (now that I knew a bit about the world) the entire thing is a bit easier to understand. Plus, I really enjoyed seeing the characters again!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503350709ra/23654299.gif' width='400' height='175' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>This one was a bit different than the last book because, besides all of the political intrigue, there was also an Invasion of the Body Snatchers flavor to it!<br/><b>What</b></span>
  <span id="freeText10325012280959640682" style="display:none">If you were on the fence about the first book (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1955069041" rel="nofollow noopener">Furies of Calderon</a>) then go ahead and give this one a try. The pacing was faster, there are finally <i>some</i> explanations for the way the furies work, and (now that I knew a bit about the world) the entire thing is a bit easier to understand. Plus, I really enjoyed seeing the characters again!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503350709ra/23654299.gif" width="400" height="175" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>This one was a bit different than the last book because, besides all of the political intrigue, there was also an Invasion of the Body Snatchers flavor to it!<br><b>What the what?!</b><br>I know, right?<br>But it was really cool!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503350709ra/23654300.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>So not only is everyone in danger from all the <i>normal</i> backstabbing that comes along with an attempted coup but now our heroes have to try to convince everyone that there's an alien life form that...well, Invades your Body and Snatches your mind!<br>Ahhhhhhh!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503350709ra/23654301.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>And they're being led by these creepy-ass bug queens...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503350709ra/23654302.gif" width="400" height="175" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Toss in some really sweet (and in Tavi's case, kind of hilarious at times) romance and mix it all together to make a really fun story. <br><b>I'm sold!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503350709ra/23654303.gif" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I'm also guessing that if you <i>didn't</i> like this one, it's probably best to put this series down and move on to something else. For me, though? This is staying a top priority.</span>

<div id="review_1386587762" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1386587762" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1386587762?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1386587762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer436725832664945702"><b>Minor spoilers follow</b> as it is impossible to talk about the plot of the second book of the series without at least mentioning some characters indicating they survived to live by the beginning of the second one. <br/><br/>Two years have passed since the events of the first book in the world with magic inspired by very popular Pokemon franchise <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442506184i/16244853.png' width='240' height='170' alt='Snorlax' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>with social structure coming straight from Ancient Rome. Thanks to a brilliant stroke by the First Lord (the Big Guy in charge of everything in the realm - for those</span>
  <span id="freeText436725832664945702" style="display:none"><b>Minor spoilers follow</b> as it is impossible to talk about the plot of the second book of the series without at least mentioning some characters indicating they survived to live by the beginning of the second one. <br><br>Two years have passed since the events of the first book in the world with magic inspired by very popular Pokemon franchise <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442506184i/16244853.png" width="240" height="170" alt="Snorlax" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>with social structure coming straight from Ancient Rome. Thanks to a brilliant stroke by the First Lord (the Big Guy in charge of everything in the realm - for those unfamiliar with the series) in political maneuvering the main characters of the first book - a former shepherd boy Tavi and his foster parents - now have to support the First Lord at all cost whether they like it or not. <br><br>So Tavi studies in the capital's Academy, his aunt stays at her steadhold (a glorified huge farm), and his uncle is in charge of local military unit. Their world is not exactly a very peaceful place; in fact the only one more dangerous I can think of is David Gemmell's Drenai. Anyway, a new almost alien threat appeared - straight from John Carpenter's movie The Thing. Now the three people I mentioned and their sidekicks are the only defense of the realm against total destruction. Do I need to say none of trio has any superpowers? Tavi cannot even use any magic at all. <br><b>Minor spoilers end here.</b><br><br>One third of the book was spent on hinting at gloomy and apocalyptic things to come. While the plot moved alone with a decent pace without losing any momentum I still got bored. I cannot even explain the reason for this, I just did. <br><br>I was sure this would have 3-star rating until I hit the second third of the tale when plot switched from fast moving to flying (supersonic aircraft style) mode. Once things began moving they really moved with people escaping extremely dangerous situations by inches only to end up in much worse ones. This reminded me of one of my favorite quotes by Robert Asprin: <br><i>"When things are at their blackest, I say to myself, 'Cheer up, things could be worse.' And sure enough, they get worse."</i><br>At this point my resolve to give 3 stars started to get weaker. And then I hit the last third of the book. <br><br>That portion of the novel contained such a nice and absolutely unexpected twist that I forgave the part where I got bored, I forgave the use of typical and worn-out classic fantasy tropes, I forgave killing off a fascinating character just when (s)he was getting some screen time, I forgave Tavi becoming the Wonder Boy for no apparent reason, I forgave countless other things. This was good enough for me to warrant 4 stars. <br><br>Before I conclude my review,<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442505509i/16244740._SX540_.png" width="240" height="170" alt="Columbo" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The first book could almost be considered standalone ad it finishes practically all the plot points. This one albeit without cliffhanger at the end, still has enough dangling threads to knit a sweater for a medium-sized elephant. Among other things this means that if you made it this far it is too late to stop now - and it applies to me as well. <br><br>My special thanks go to my friend Jaime for the ideal Pokemon image idea:)</span>
  <a data-text-id="436725832664945702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText10448700473864828101" style="display:none">I liked Furies of Calderon (the first book in the Codex Alera series) but thought it was pretty average compared to other works in the genre. It delivered on every promise made in the first book and completely blew me away with its stellar pacing, fantastic battle scenes, exceptional characters, and overall creativity. I felt like my heart was ripped out a few times while reading it and I love it when a book can make me feel that engaged. I already liked Jim Butcher, but this book launched him forward a few more notches in my book.<br><br>If I had any criticisms, it’s that the main character was sometimes more suave and resourceful in difficult situations than I thought believable… but it did make for some excellent and memorable moments, so I won’t complain too much. :-)<br><br>Overall, if you are on the fence with whether to start the series or continue on after the first book (like I was), take it from me – totally worth it!<br><br>Via The Obsessive Bookseller at <a href="http://www.NikiHawkes.com" rel="nofollow noopener">www.NikiHawkes.com</a> <br><br>Other books you might like:<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6765788.The_Last_Stormlord__Watergivers___1_" title="The Last Stormlord (Watergivers, #1) by Glenda Larke" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_439848470" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/439848470" />
    <a title="Tom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7476704-tom"><img alt="Tom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1333052331p2/7476704.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/439848470?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tom" href="/user/show/7476704-tom">Tom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer439848470" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9822634937658202592">Another action packed installment of a great fantasy series. <br/><br/> I didn't know where it where it was going to go after the first book but was floored when it was every bit as good as Furies of Calderon and possibly exceeding it. In Academ’s Fury we get to see Tavi grow as he studies to be a Cursor. We get multiple stories going again with many of the characters from the first book. In addition we are introduced to some new intriguing characters one of my favorites being Tavi’s best friend Max. Kita</span>
  <span id="freeText9822634937658202592" style="display:none">Another action packed installment of a great fantasy series. <br /><br /> I didn't know where it where it was going to go after the first book but was floored when it was every bit as good as Furies of Calderon and possibly exceeding it. In Academ’s Fury we get to see Tavi grow as he studies to be a Cursor. We get multiple stories going again with many of the characters from the first book. In addition we are introduced to some new intriguing characters one of my favorites being Tavi’s best friend Max. Kitai makes an appearance and she is just the perfect heroine. <br /><br />This is the second book of the series so I can only say so much about it without giving things away. But what I love most about this series, besides the writing, is that it always has you thinking. The political villains in this series aren't Snidley Whiplash obvious villains. You start to see their side of issues and it makes it difficult to decide where your allegiance should lie. I love when a story makes you think about which side of the road is the evil. In this series most of the politicians fall in the grey zone. There is one group that is definitely the evil party but from there it is hard to decide whose team to root for. Although this is much more action/adventure there are some romances that are sprouting from the series but it is happening in a very believable atmosphere. The only negative is unlike the first book bouncing between stories was cliffier. Maybe that was just because there wasn't any breaks throughout the whole book.<br /><br />If you are into Fantasy, like great writing, and don’t need the steamy, you really need to pick up this series. It’s not very often that I pick up a 600 page fantasy book and don’t have to skim.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9822634937658202592" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2869941764" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2869941764" />
    <a title="⋆  yel  ⋆" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36155695-yel"><img alt="⋆  yel  ⋆" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603643156p2/36155695.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2869941764?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="⋆  yel  ⋆" class="user" itemprop="url" name="⋆  yel  ⋆" href="/user/show/36155695-yel">⋆  yel  ⋆</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36155695-yel?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36155695-yel?shelf=review">review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36155695-yel?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2869941764" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16392448480044360457"><i>
  <b> 4.25 of 5 stars<br/><br/>-----</b>
</i><br/><br/>Omg, this book! I definitely loved this more than the first book! I certainly loved the political aspect as the main focus of this series. It always excites me whenever a story involves political mind games and battleground techniques. I specifically loved this because of the slow but intense world building. The dreadful battles didn't last for just a few pages, but span for almost half the book. Those battles kept me on the edge of my seat the whole time. There was more</span>
  <span id="freeText16392448480044360457" style="display:none"><i>
  <b> 4.25 of 5 stars<br /><br />-----</b>
</i><br /><br />Omg, this book! I definitely loved this more than the first book! I certainly loved the political aspect as the main focus of this series. It always excites me whenever a story involves political mind games and battleground techniques. I specifically loved this because of the slow but intense world building. The dreadful battles didn't last for just a few pages, but span for almost half the book. Those battles kept me on the edge of my seat the whole time. There was more than enough tension set up for a whole book.<br /><br />Aside from that, there's so much character development, especially Tavi. Oh my, Tavi! I remember that there was not enough scenes of him on the first book and I was so glad we had more of him on this one. I can proudly say that he became one of my most favorite male fictional characters ever. Among the several character perspective, Tavi was the one I'm most looking forward to. He was so smart, courageous, caring and rational. I loved that despite being furyless, he's the most capable among all of them. He didn't let his emotions cloud his judgements. In fact, he can think more rational when he feels things. I can practically hear how his mind works whenever he was in a helpless position. He was also wise and politically knowledgeable. That scene when he was almost too late to get to the Citadel to save the First Lord and hopeless about not having enough help, his <i>'the enemy of my enemy is my friend'</i> clever plan was not something I can think of myself! The fact that the fate of the Realm relies literally on his decisions was too much I actually felt bad for him. Oh my, I loved his character so much! <br /><br />If Tavi was my most favorite character in this series, Isana was one of my least favorite. It already crept my mind in the first book. I don't like how she handled things. I almost always disagree with her decisions. She was the exact opposite of Tavi when it comes to formulating steps and decisions. She always let her emotions affect her judgement. I mean, I respect her for having so much love and care for her loved ones, her desire to protect them and do everything to make them safe, but she often decides without thinking beyond that. I can't exactly blame her, especially when I discovered something from her words at the end of the book. But still. I always don't like unwise characters. And I noticed that she always missed the important battles, even in the first book. There's always something going on with her and her lack of participation in those battles made me think about her less. <br /><br />Overall, this is a very intense book. So much happened and I enjoyed every last bit of them. Those last few pages made me speculate a lot of things. I'm so excited for the next book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16392448480044360457" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_251185743" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/251185743" />
    <a title="Kaila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3335221-kaila"><img alt="Kaila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525808775p2/3335221.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/251185743?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaila" href="/user/show/3335221-kaila">Kaila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335221-kaila?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335221-kaila?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335221-kaila?shelf=fantasy-aficionados-challenge-2012">fantasy-aficionados-challenge-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335221-kaila?shelf=magic">magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer251185743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17103910151493154986">Although this installment was easier for me to read than <i>Furies of Calderon</i> (my groans were cut down by about a third, I'd say), I liked this second novel no more than the first one. It has been two years since the events of <i>Furies</i>, and we're plopped right back into the action without so much as an update, which at first had me a little miffed. The problem with plowing through novels so quickly is that proper nouns quickly find their way into the oubliette, so even though it's only been about tw</span>
  <span id="freeText17103910151493154986" style="display:none">Although this installment was easier for me to read than <i>Furies of Calderon</i> (my groans were cut down by about a third, I'd say), I liked this second novel no more than the first one. It has been two years since the events of <i>Furies</i>, and we're plopped right back into the action without so much as an update, which at first had me a little miffed. The problem with plowing through novels so quickly is that proper nouns quickly find their way into the oubliette, so even though it's only been about two months, I was still playing catch up trying to remember who the characters were. <br /><br />On second thought, let's not blame me. The names just aren't very memorable. I was 3/4s of the way through this book and explaining it to a friend and I had to grope for the main character's name. T...t...it's T-something I swear! Tavi? No wonder he's powerless, he <i>sounds</i> like it. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yes yes, I can finally easily remember his name now that I know his full name, Octavian. I cared so little about this series that the not so subtle hints went right over my head. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />From the first page, Butcher sets up the story, and from there on out it is non-stop action. I like a good action scene as much as the next bloke, but in this case it really started to grate on me. The characters are never given a chance for introspection, besides sparing a thought or two for "I wonder where this other character is right now? No matter, off to another near death situation!" So once again, one of my main problems is the lack of character development. I know what the author <i>wants</i> the characters to be, but they never seem to get there on their own. We're just told they do, and I am baffled at people who say these characters feel "alive." Only alive in the sense that fire is alive; expanding the story and going new places but leaving nothing behind to appreciate. Honestly, the only character I felt became a little more interesting in this novel was Fidelias, who I <i>hated</i> in the first book, so that's saying a lot. I always like it when bad guys become likable.<br /><br />What really interests me about this series is the weak (well, relatively) main character. Tavi uses his brains and quick wit to talk himself out of - or into - situations. Usually in fantasy novels, any sort of magic is regarded with suspicion, à la X-Men. Someone with crazy powers and inhuman strength is usually incredibly frightening to the layman. In these novels, however, Tavi is the <i>only</i> weak character without magic, and <i>he's</i> the weirdo and regarded with suspicion. This flips my thoughts on magic and powers on its head, and I like that. I can't help but be gut wrenchingly involved whenever Tavi is in the middle of the action. I always want THIS to be the moment when his powers manifest.<br /><br />I could have done without the weird women's rights story line. I know I know, I'm always touting about how sexist fantasy is and give me my strong female characters dammit. But in this case, it just came across as schmaltzy and a thoroughly fake story line to throw some pretend politics into the mix. Without it, there would have been next to no politics in the novel, and Butcher obviously wants us to be aware of the political situation in the realm.<br /><br />The love story between Amara and Bernard was uncomfortable at best and gag worthy at worst. Here's my favorite quote from page 453:<br /><br /><blockquote>Amara let out a nervous little laugh, and her cheeks flushed hot. She took two steps to Bernard and leaned up to kiss him again. He returned it, one hand touching her waist, a possessive gesture.</blockquote><br /><br /><i>Please!</i> Hopefully it picks up a little in subsequent books.<br /><br />Pick this up if you want a fun romp with non stop action, with little consequence but also small reward. It definitely improves on the first novel, but not enough for me to legitimately like it on its own.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17103910151493154986" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1671266661" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1671266661" />
    <a title="Philip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30863291-philip"><img alt="Philip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527983001p2/30863291.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1671266661?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Philip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Philip" href="/user/show/30863291-philip">Philip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1671266661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2360252918323094530">3.5ish stars.<br/><br/>Book #2 provided a lot of what I loved about book #1, added a few more things that I love and, unfortunately, a few things I didn't love as well. Possible spoilers to follow.<br/><br/>The first chapter led me to believe that the series had gone waaay downhill somewhere in the gap between where the last book ended and this one began. Literally every stupid high school cliche I've ever read in one chapter- poor Tavi and his nerdy friends are getting bullied by the bigger, stronger more popular </span>
  <span id="freeText2360252918323094530" style="display:none">3.5ish stars.<br /><br />Book #2 provided a lot of what I loved about book #1, added a few more things that I love and, unfortunately, a few things I didn't love as well. Possible spoilers to follow.<br /><br />The first chapter led me to believe that the series had gone waaay downhill somewhere in the gap between where the last book ended and this one began. Literally every stupid high school cliche I've ever read in one chapter- poor Tavi and his nerdy friends are getting bullied by the bigger, stronger more popular kids! Oh wait! Someone even bigger and stronger comes in to save the day and humiliate the bullies! What a lucky coincidence! Ugh. I'm glad that ended quickly. I realize that this is a classic high fantasy novel and there are certain tropes that are to be expected, even loved, but I like it so much more when Butcher transcends the particularly cheesy ones in his writing.<br /><br />Despite what I was initially led to believe, Tavi actually became a better, more likeable character this time around. One of my criticisms of Furies of Calderon was the flat characterizations, Tavi included. I think he really came into his own here and I'm glad that Butcher hasn't (yet, at least) sold out and gifted Tavi with furycrafting abilities. He's way cooler and more interesting without them. Also, he pretty much (inexplicably) saved the realm again without any of those abilities. Pretty ridiculous but also pretty B.A.<br /><br />One thing that was true about the first book and continues to be true here is that all of the "good" characters, the protagonists, are so <i>gooood</i>. There's none of the moral ambiguity that makes a really great protagonist. Bernard and Amara and Tavi are just so <i>noble</i> (spoken in the voice of Hades from Hercules). Boring! Isana, ever the victim, did have some interesting developments but only because she's so <i>noble</i>. Boring! All of the interesting characters who played both sides of the good/evil field, like Fidelias, Gaius, Varg, Lady Aquitane, etc. were ones that we saw for like five minutes every once in a while before we went back to the <i>noble</i> ones. Boring! On a side note- favorite character? Kitai.<br /><br />Butcher did a lot to expand the world of Alera by introducing a lot of political intrigue and moving the setting from rural Calderon to the big city of Alera Imperia in the heart of the country. It made things feel a lot bigger and more epic and dramatic. <br /><br />Call me wishy-washy but something cheesy that I did love was the romance. Tavi and Kitai! *heart eyes* Amara and Bernard! *heart eyes* Max and Gaius's wife! *heart eyes* Let's hook Isana up with someone here! The poor woman is lonely! <br /><br />Was it just me or is this significantly longer than Furies of Calderon? It felt overlong and there were a few parts I struggled through despite the generally quick pace. I'm really looking forward to book 3, but I think I'll have to take a little break before I begin.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2360252918323094530" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7492998228817049774">Academ's Fury was a truly excellent book. The characters all showed great depth, the struggles they faced kept me tearing through the pages to see what happened next, and the new dangers <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[The Vord and Canim <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> were terrifying.<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[The situations that all the POV characters found themselves in was tense to say it nicely. It was shocking and pleasing to see alliances change as Isanna joined The Aquataines in order to protect her family. I enjoyed Bernard and Am</span></span>
  <span id="freeText7492998228817049774" style="display:none">Academ's Fury was a truly excellent book. The characters all showed great depth, the struggles they faced kept me tearing through the pages to see what happened next, and the new dangers <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The Vord and Canim <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> were terrifying.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The situations that all the POV characters found themselves in was tense to say it nicely. It was shocking and pleasing to see alliances change as Isanna joined The Aquataines in order to protect her family. I enjoyed Bernard and Amara relationship struggles and last second marriage all while they were nearly exterminated by the Vord. I'm also a big fan of Antillar Maximus who I envision playing a large part in the story to come.<br /><br />I also appreciated the harsh realities faced in this book that those taken by the Vord couldn't be saved. Part of me kept expecting that once the Vord Queen was killed that everyone would go back to normal. Though I felt horrid particularly for Aric and Heddy I thought it was better that they couldn't come back once the Queen was killed.<br /><br />One thing struck me as odd though...the Vord take over basically anyone and everyone yet it appeared Ambassador Varg's second Sarl was an accomplice rather than one of the taken. I wonder if that will be expanded on later or if there is no real importance to it. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I wish I could say more, but even with the spoilers I feel like I'm giving away too much of the story. I'm definitely looking forward to starting to the next book in the series.</span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review890879496">
  <td colspan="2">

  <span id="freeText8372212172868368050" style="display:none">When the first Lord of Alera Gaius mysteriously falls unconscious after drinking Spirit fire, Tavi and his friends must come up with a plan to cover for the ill Lord before the realm ends up in chaos. <div id="review_2155113817" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2155113817" />
    <a title="Steven Naylor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36735178-steven-naylor"><img alt="Steven Naylor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532291169p2/36735178.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2155113817?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steven Naylor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steven Naylor" href="/user/show/36735178-steven-naylor">Steven Naylor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2155113817" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3060895675337188536">Rating a solid 4 stars<br/><br/> I like these books much better than I like the Dresden books. Between the Dresden books and now the Codex Alera books I have come to the conclusion that Jim Butcher has an over-the-top writing style. There is basically non-stop action throughout all his books. One could argue that there is almost too much action. What I mean by over-the-top writing style is that he makes the odds against the good guys terrible from the beginning and then throughout the story makes them wor</span>
  <span id="freeText3060895675337188536" style="display:none">Rating a solid 4 stars<br /><br /> I like these books much better than I like the Dresden books. Between the Dresden books and now the Codex Alera books I have come to the conclusion that Jim Butcher has an over-the-top writing style. There is basically non-stop action throughout all his books. One could argue that there is almost too much action. What I mean by over-the-top writing style is that he makes the odds against the good guys terrible from the beginning and then throughout the story makes them worse and worse. It seems a little redundant to make an impossible task even more difficult. I enjoyed reading about the fighting and the different ways in which the magic can be used. However, in my mind I am trying to keep track of the odds and how the overall fight is progressing, and in my mind what is being described is impossible. There are multiple battles both in this book and the first book with many waves in the fighting. Keeping track of the total number of people fighting from the beginning, and the number of people lost during each skirmish, would have left no people able to fight a long time ago. So, while there is great heroism in the fighting and I do think the fight scenes are very well written, I don't think they are very realistic. However, since I know that going into the story, I can just go along with it and enjoy the book - which I did. <br /><br /> The story takes place 2 years after the last book. Tavi is in the capitol studying to be a cursor. I love all stories that talk about training and how things are done. To be honest I wish the story had more on this subject, because again it is one of my favorite parts of any story. Tavi's Uncle Bernard also has a big part in this story as well as his Aunt Isana. Without giving too much away, Everyone is in trouble at the same time and needs help. Some of the problems are related and some of them are separate, which just coincidentally happen at the same time (see what I mean about over-the-top story telling?). <br /><br /> By not focusing too much on the impossibility of the story, I was able to sit back and enjoy it much more. While I do think Jim Butcher does a great job at "in the moment" writing, I don't think he does a great job at intrigue. Or to be more specific, I think I can see from a mile away where the story is going (at least on a big picture sort of way). I think I have figured out, even before starting this book, the secrets that are being kept. I also wish the Jim Butcher would spend a little more time on world building as the world that he has created is so interesting. I just think it could use a little more detail. He does do a great job with his characters though, and I really feel for the people that he has created. <br /><br />Overall this book is better than the first one and while not perfect, it is a very good read and I look forward to reading the next book in the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3060895675337188536" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_416217540" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/416217540" />
    <a title="Jonathan Terrington" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6313408-jonathan-terrington"><img alt="Jonathan Terrington" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478230200p2/6313408.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/416217540?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jonathan Terrington" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jonathan Terrington" href="/user/show/6313408-jonathan-terrington">Jonathan Terrington</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=worldbuilding">worldbuilding</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=favourite-series">favourite-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer416217540" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer457465177003345757">Jim Butcher's first two books in his Codex Alera are fascinating - weighted with capable, yet flawed female and male characters, and full of political intrigue and adventure. The very concept: an alien world populated by future descendants of the Roman people is intriguing. However, at times the writing itself feels 'too neat' and the suspension of disbelief falters.<br/><br/>The book follows Tavi, a young man in a world of furycrafters, who cannot furycraft. Furycrafting is the magic system of this world</span>
  <span id="freeText457465177003345757" style="display:none">Jim Butcher's first two books in his Codex Alera are fascinating - weighted with capable, yet flawed female and male characters, and full of political intrigue and adventure. The very concept: an alien world populated by future descendants of the Roman people is intriguing. However, at times the writing itself feels 'too neat' and the suspension of disbelief falters.<br /><br />The book follows Tavi, a young man in a world of furycrafters, who cannot furycraft. Furycrafting is the magic system of this world, whereby each citizen has possession of one or more elemental spirits called furies. This concept is of course, based upon the Roman mythologies and the concept of the one 'freak hero' in a world of magic who has none himself. In this book in particular, however, the reader witnesses the development of Tavi as a man - whereas in the first book he was a young adolescent. This develops Tavi as an interesting character and leads the reader to want to follow his journey onwards across the continuing novels.<br /><br />As far as fantasy works travel this is a 'nice' book. It is a neat distraction that allows the reader to pass away the time without every being anything grander. Yet it is for this reason that the novel works entirely. It is polished escapism.<br /><br /> At times Jim Butcher weighs his story and world down with various political machinations which add a depth of realism to his characters and story but which drag down the entertainment value. Which leads me to consider that I must complete the entire series before making an appropriate judgement of where the entire narrative is leading towards. </span>
  <a data-text-id="457465177003345757" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2810545639" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2810545639" />
    <a title="Nadine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3759963-nadine"><img alt="Nadine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566849081p2/3759963.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2810545639?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nadine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nadine" href="/user/show/3759963-nadine">Nadine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2810545639" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3122138009748804105">Academ’s Fury is the sequel to the Furies of Calderon though it doesn’t necessarily read like a sequel. Full of action, political intrigue, and characters I will now follow to the ends of the earth, the Codex Alera is a series I’m now committed to 100%. <br/> <br/>As I mentioned previously, Academ’s Fury does not read like a sequel for the most part because of the nature of the plot. The novel follows Tavi as he navigates school and training to become a Cursor. With this type of plot comes the typical tro</span>
  <span id="freeText3122138009748804105" style="display:none">Academ’s Fury is the sequel to the Furies of Calderon though it doesn’t necessarily read like a sequel. Full of action, political intrigue, and characters I will now follow to the ends of the earth, the Codex Alera is a series I’m now committed to 100%. <br /> <br />As I mentioned previously, Academ’s Fury does not read like a sequel for the most part because of the nature of the plot. The novel follows Tavi as he navigates school and training to become a Cursor. With this type of plot comes the typical tropes of attending boarding school. Butcher does a fantastic job of keeping the tropes fresh and exciting through the richness of the characters and plot established previously in the first novel. <br /> <br />Academ’s Fury is action packed and full of political intrigue. Each chapter oscillates between different points of view, primarily Tavi, Amara, and Isana. So, readers get the best of each story unfolding in each perspective. Through Tavi, readers get the typical fantasy boarding school story. Through Amara, readers get a look at the bigger picture. And Through Isana, readers get a glimpse of the political machinations that drive this world. <br /> <br />What I enjoy most about this series is the characters. They’re fleshed out, rich in detail, and full of personality. It’s hard to point to a favorite since they all embody qualities I love to read about in characters, but Kitai and Tavi’s connection is one I’m most excited to explore in the next book, especially with how things end in Academ’s Fury. <br /><br />Gaius reminds me of Dumbledore. He shows up as an all-powerful character dolling out wisdom and nuggets of important information only to be taken off the board until the end of the novel. I’m excited to see more of him, though I think he’ll suffer a similar fate as Dumbledore. <br /><br />Overall, Academ’s Fury has cemented my love for this series through its incredible characters and fast-moving plot with twists and turns I didn’t see coming. I cannot wait to get my copy of Cursor’s Fury. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3122138009748804105" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_362649693" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/362649693" />
    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10743961-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422270416p2/10743961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/362649693?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/10743961-rob">Rob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=author-male">author-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-before-goodreads">read-before-goodreads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer362649693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1172290844597997387"><b>Executive Summary:</b> The chosen one goes to school in the capital and politics abound! If you enjoyed the first book, I think you'll find a lot to like here as Mr. Butcher continues to build out the world from the first book.<br/><br/><b>Audio book:</b> Kate Reading once more does a great job as a reader. I've gotten used to her reading all the male voices so it's much less noticeable.<br/><br/>One of her voices in this one is so spot on to what I imagined, I find it annoying (because I find the way that character talks to </span>
  <span id="freeText1172290844597997387" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> The chosen one goes to school in the capital and politics abound! If you enjoyed the first book, I think you'll find a lot to like here as Mr. Butcher continues to build out the world from the first book.<br /><br /><b>Audio book:</b> Kate Reading once more does a great job as a reader. I've gotten used to her reading all the male voices so it's much less noticeable.<br /><br />One of her voices in this one is so spot on to what I imagined, I find it annoying (because I find the way that character talks to be annoying). Doing the audiobooks for this series aren't a must like Mr. Butcher's Dresden Files, but they certainly aren't a bad option in my opinion.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />Like the last book, this one started a little slow for me. It also leans heavily on tropes. We get a bit of the magical school trope here, though not a lot of it. For me that's a bad thing, because it's one of the reason I like Harry Potter so much.<br /><br />Then again when your protagonist has no magical abilities to speak of, I guess it makes little sense to dwell on the magical training that takes place there. Instead most of the focus is on politics between not only the various Aleran factions, but also with the Canim, a fierce wolf-like race who despite being considered enemies of the Alerans, maintain an embassy in the capital. This leads to one of my favorite characters of the series, Ambassador Varg.<br /><br />This book also introduces my other favorite in Antillar Maximus. His antics remind me a bit of Harry Dresden and add some levity that was mostly lacking from the first novel.<br /><br />Now what magical school story would be complete without the asshole bully, that I like to call "The Malfoy"? (I know Harry Potter wasn't the first to use this trope, but its arguably the most popular). Tavi must deal with bullying on a more severe scale than he ever faced back home in the form of Kalarus Brencis Minoris, son of High Lord Kalarus and his two cronies. Is it a requirement the bully have exactly 2 cronies? It certainly seems like it.<br /><br />The stereotypical bully isn't the only thing of concern here however, and there are once again shades of gray when it comes to just who is "good" and who is "bad", all rolled up into the politics between nobles that are the most powerful in more than just title. Seriously, you do not want to be trapped in a dark alley with a High Lord or Lady whose pissed at you. It won't end well.<br /><br />The story is also split with events back in the Calderon valley. I found that subplot a bit slow/uninteresting on this re-read, although Doroga helps to make it worthwhile and the second half of that story is a lot more enjoyable than the first.<br /><br />Overall I found there is a lot I like here, in particular the politics and some of the new characters, that help me get over some of the slower parts of the story.<br /><br />On to book 3, which is one of my all-time favorites!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1172290844597997387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1066773848?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ctgt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ctgt" href="/user/show/3787451-ctgt">Ctgt</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3787451-ctgt?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1066773848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer434825838874293324">I don't spend much time on reviews for later books in series' and this won't be any exception. If it's utter garbage then I'll lay out more details but as you can tell from my rating, I enjoyed this second book in the series. It had been quite a few months since I read the first book so I was a little concerned about getting back into the world. It took a few chapters but fairly quickly I was thrust back into Alera with Tavi, Bernard, Amara, Isana and my favorites, Doroga and Walker. Some politi</span>
  <span id="freeText434825838874293324" style="display:none">I don't spend much time on reviews for later books in series' and this won't be any exception. If it's utter garbage then I'll lay out more details but as you can tell from my rating, I enjoyed this second book in the series. It had been quite a few months since I read the first book so I was a little concerned about getting back into the world. It took a few chapters but fairly quickly I was thrust back into Alera with Tavi, Bernard, Amara, Isana and my favorites, Doroga and Walker. Some political intrigue, elemental magic, an ancient nemesis of the Marat and the writing style really moved this story along at a brisk pace. I'll definitely be continuing on with the series.<br /><br />3.5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="434825838874293324" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1851670426" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1851670426" />
    <a title="Sheyla ✎" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4627974-sheyla"><img alt="Sheyla ✎" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550756072p2/4627974.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1851670426?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sheyla ✎" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sheyla ✎" href="/user/show/4627974-sheyla">Sheyla ✎</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781440656897" href="/book/show/9866750-academ-s-fury">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4627974-sheyla?shelf=5-fangs">5-fangs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4627974-sheyla?shelf=audible">audible</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4627974-sheyla?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4627974-sheyla?shelf=amazing-series">amazing-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1851670426" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8024652700240511328"><a href='https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-CFACe9SN6k4/WGMKIaGZRBI/AAAAAAAAP1g/JZ-1ALRYmDs63E3NwGOBOBwkg6SkS3QzgCLcB/s1600/luv.gif' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img height='218' src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1482885682ra/21557871.gif' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>
  <blockquote>“Anger subsides. Love doesn’t.”</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/>What an excellent second book! Just as good or better than the first. If I had one word to describe this book, I would use the adjective <b>EXCILERANT</b>! <br/><br/>Jim Butcher is a master at crafting a unique world where amazing characters live. I wish I could join them. Maybe even have my own furies too. Who wouldn't want to meet Doroga, Tavi, Isana, Gaius, Bernard, or Kitai? I certainly would. <br/><br/><b>
  <blockquote>“Your Kind, Aleran, are the most vicious and gentle, most savage and noble</blockquote></b></span>
  <span id="freeText8024652700240511328" style="display:none"><a href="https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-CFACe9SN6k4/WGMKIaGZRBI/AAAAAAAAP1g/JZ-1ALRYmDs63E3NwGOBOBwkg6SkS3QzgCLcB/s1600/luv.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="218" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1482885682ra/21557871.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Anger subsides. Love doesn’t.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>What an excellent second book! Just as good or better than the first. If I had one word to describe this book, I would use the adjective <b>EXCILERANT</b>! <br><br>Jim Butcher is a master at crafting a unique world where amazing characters live. I wish I could join them. Maybe even have my own furies too. Who wouldn't want to meet Doroga, Tavi, Isana, Gaius, Bernard, or Kitai? I certainly would. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Your Kind, Aleran, are the most vicious and gentle, most savage and noble, most treacherous and loyal, most terrifying and fascinating creatures I have ever seen.”</blockquote>
</b> <br><br>So what else does Jim do? He gives us even more awesome characters like Max, Killian, and Gargant. Of course, he also throws in the mix great evil too. We have Lord Attis Aquitaine and Lord Kalarus Brencis fighting to overthrown Gaius Sextus while the Vord's Queens' are creating nests and reproducing. Tavi with the help of friends will have to fight them at the palace while Bernard, Doroga, and Amara will join forces to do it in the valley. This leaves Isana desperate to forge an alliance to be able to help her family, even if this new alliance could change the power balance. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“You will probably find, in life, that successes and victories tend to overshadow the risks you took, while failure will amplify how idiotic they were.”</blockquote>
</b> <br><br>Academ's Fury is a fast-paced fantasy. It's heavy on the action but like with Dresden, there is always time for humor and romance. Furthermore, there were a few twists. Some of them I saw them coming, others took me by surprise. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Doroga thumped a finger against his skull. Head got nothing to do with the heart. Your heart wants what it wants. Head got to learn that it can only kill the heart or else get out of the way”</blockquote>
</b> <br><br>I can't wait to see what the future brings for Tavi. It can only get more complicated and deadly for him. I do hope that most of the main characters survive. I have a soft spot for a lot of them. <br><br>5/5 <b>"Aleran"</b> Fangs<br><br><a href="http://www.mrsleifs.com/2016/12/academs-fury-by-jim-butcher.html" rel="nofollow noopener">MrsLeif's Two Fangs About It</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/MrsLeifsbookreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/MrsLeifs_2Fangs" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/booksrmyworld/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8024652700240511328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer765531284" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7919169490093383891">I gave this series a good second chance to win me over. There are many reasons why it didn't succeed:<br/><br/>Potboiler romance, shallow characters without development, predictable story is the best I can say. Though it's packed with action, it feels repetitive and you have to search for worthwile and important scenes. I had to skim through the pages to endure and reach the end. <br/>I hoped for world building and interesting developments of the furies' magic system - but in 700 pages, nearly nothing new was </span>
  <span id="freeText7919169490093383891" style="display:none">I gave this series a good second chance to win me over. There are many reasons why it didn't succeed:<br /><br />Potboiler romance, shallow characters without development, predictable story is the best I can say. Though it's packed with action, it feels repetitive and you have to search for worthwile and important scenes. I had to skim through the pages to endure and reach the end. <br />I hoped for world building and interesting developments of the furies' magic system - but in 700 pages, nearly nothing new was unccovered.<br />Instead, we find standard fantasy tropes like magic school bullying that have been described better elsewhere.<br />The rest of the series is predictable, as well - already the titles suggest Tavi's coming of age: In the next novel he'll be cursor, then captain, prince and finally first lord.<br />I'll throw the series out of my shelves.<br /></span>
